## The Saá¹…gÄ«ti Sutta

296. Evaá¹ƒ me sutaá¹ƒ â€“ ekaá¹ƒ samayaá¹ƒ bhagavÄ mallesu cÄrikaá¹ƒ caramÄno mahatÄ bhikkhusaá¹…ghena saddhiá¹ƒ paÃ±camattehi bhikkhusatehi yena pÄvÄ nÄma mallÄnaá¹ƒ nagaraá¹ƒ tadavasari. Tatra sudaá¹ƒ bhagavÄ pÄvÄyaá¹ƒ viharati cundassa kammÄraputtassa ambavane.

296.Thus have I heard. At one time the Blessed One was traveling among the Mallas with a large company of monks, with some five hundred monks, and arrived at PÄvÄ, a town of the Mallas. There the Blessed One was dwelling in PÄvÄ, in the mango grove of Cunda the metalworker's son.

297.At that time, the Mallas of PÄvÄ had a newly built assembly hall called Ubbhataka, which had not yet been occupied by any ascetic, brahmin, or any human being. The Blessed One consented in silence.

298.Then the Mallas of PÄvÄ, understanding the Blessed Oneâ€™s acceptance, rose from their seats, paid homage to him, circumambulated him, and went to the assembly hall. Standing to one side, the Mallas of PÄvÄ said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, the assembly hall is entirely spread with mats, seats have been arranged for the Blessed One, a water vessel has been set up, and an oil lamp has been lit. 299.Then the Blessed One, having dressed, taken his bowl and robe, went to the assembly hall together with the Saá¹…gha of monks. The Saá¹…gha of monks also washed their feet, entered the assembly hall, and sat down facing east, leaning against the western wall, keeping the Blessed One in front of them. The Mallas of PÄvÄ also washed their feet, entered the assembly hall, and sat down facing west, leaning against the eastern wall, keeping the Blessed One in front of them. You may do what seems fit to you now." "Yes, venerable sir," the Mallas of PÄvÄ replied to the Blessed One. Then they rose from their seats, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed.

300. 300.Then, not long after the Mallas of PÄvÄ had left, the Blessed One surveyed the silent Saá¹…gha of monks and addressed Venerable SÄriputta: "The Saá¹…gha of monks is free from dullness and drowsiness, SÄriputta. ## Bhinnanigaá¹‡á¹­havatthu

### The Story of the Schism of the Nigaá¹‡á¹­has

301. Tena kho pana samayena nigaá¹‡á¹­ho nÄá¹­aputto pÄvÄyaá¹ƒ adhunÄkÄlaá¹…kato hoti. Adhiciá¹‡á¹‡aá¹ƒ te viparÄvattaá¹ƒ, Äropito te vÄdo, niggahito tvamasi, cara vÄdappamokkhÄya, nibbeá¹­hehi vÄ sace pahosÄ«â€™â€™ti. Vadhoyeva kho maÃ±Ã±e nigaá¹‡á¹­hesu nÄá¹­aputtiyesu vattati. Yepi [yepi te (sÄ«. pÄ«.)] nigaá¹‡á¹­hassa nÄá¹­aputtassa sÄvakÄ gihÄ« odÄtavasanÄ, tepi nigaá¹‡á¹­hesu nÄá¹­aputtiyesu nibbinnarÅ«pÄ virattarÅ«pÄ paá¹­ivÄnarÅ«pÄ, yathÄ taá¹ƒ durakkhÄte dhammavinaye duppavedite aniyyÄnike anupasamasaá¹ƒvattanike asammÄsambuddhappavedite bhinnathÅ«pe appaá¹­isaraá¹‡e.

301.Now on that occasion the Nigaá¹‡á¹­ha NÄá¹­aputta had recently passed away at PÄvÄ. Upon his passing away, the Nigaá¹‡á¹­has became divided into two factions, quarreling, brawling, and engaging in disputes, stabbing each other with verbal daggers: â€œYou donâ€™t understand this Dhamma and Disciplineâ€”I understand it! How could you understand this Dhamma and Discipline? Youâ€™re practicing wronglyâ€”Iâ€™m practicing rightly! What I say is consistentâ€”what you say isnâ€™t! What should be said first, you say last; what should be said last, you say first! Your long-held view is refuted! Your argument is refuted! Youâ€™re defeated! Go and disentangle your argument if you can!â€ It seems that strife was rife among the Nigaá¹‡á¹­has, the followers of NÄá¹­aputta. Even the lay disciples of Nigaá¹‡á¹­ha NÄá¹­aputta, wearing white clothes, became disillusioned, disaffected, and disgusted with the Nigaá¹‡á¹­has, seeing how poorly proclaimed was their Dhamma and Discipline, how badly expounded, not leading to liberation, not conducive to peace, not proclaimed by a Perfectly Self-Enlightened Oneâ€”with its shattered foundation and no refuge.

302. Atha kho ÄyasmÄ sÄriputto bhikkhÅ« Ämantesi â€“ â€˜â€˜nigaá¹‡á¹­ho, Ävuso, nÄá¹­aputto pÄvÄyaá¹ƒ adhunÄkÄlaá¹…kato, tassa kÄlaá¹…kiriyÄya bhinnÄ nigaá¹‡á¹­hÄ dvedhikajÄtÄâ€¦peâ€¦ bhinnathÅ«pe appaá¹­isaraá¹‡eâ€™â€™. â€˜â€˜EvaÃ±hetaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, hoti durakkhÄte dhammavinaye duppavedite aniyyÄnike anupasamasaá¹ƒvattanike asammÄsambuddhappavedite. Ayaá¹ƒ kho panÄvuso amhÄkaá¹ƒ [asmÄkaá¹ƒ (pÄ«.)] bhagavatÄ [bhagavato (ka. sÄ«.)] dhammo svÄkkhÄto suppavedito niyyÄniko upasamasaá¹ƒvattaniko sammÄsambuddhappavedito. Tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒ, na vivaditabbaá¹ƒ, yathayidaá¹ƒ brahmacariyaá¹ƒ addhaniyaá¹ƒ assa ciraá¹­á¹­hitikaá¹ƒ, tadassa bahujanahitÄya bahujanasukhÄya lokÄnukampÄya atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ.

302.Then Venerable SÄriputta addressed the bhikkhus: â€œBhikkhus, the Nigaá¹‡á¹­ha NÄá¹­aputta has recently passed away at PÄvÄ. â€˜â€˜Katamo cÄvuso, amhÄkaá¹ƒ bhagavatÄ [bhagavato (ka. sÄ«.)] dhammo svÄkkhÄto suppavedito niyyÄniko upasamasaá¹ƒvattaniko sammÄsambuddhappavedito; yattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒ, na vivaditabbaá¹ƒ, yathayidaá¹ƒ brahmacariyaá¹ƒ addhaniyaá¹ƒ assa ciraá¹­á¹­hitikaá¹ƒ, tadassa bahujanahitÄya bahujanasukhÄya lokÄnukampÄya atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ?

â€œAnd what, bhikkhus, is the Dhamma well-proclaimed by our Blessed One, well-expounded, leading to liberation, conducive to peace, proclaimed by a Perfectly Self-Enlightened One; wherein all should recite together, not dispute, so that this holy life may endure long and be long-lasting, for the welfare of the many, for the happiness of the many, out of compassion for the world, for the good, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans?â€

## Ekakaá¹ƒ

### The One

303. â€˜â€˜Atthi kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena eko dhammo sammadakkhÄto. Tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒ, na vivaditabbaá¹ƒ, yathayidaá¹ƒ brahmacariyaá¹ƒ addhaniyaá¹ƒ assa ciraá¹­á¹­hitikaá¹ƒ, tadassa bahujanahitÄya bahujanasukhÄya lokÄnukampÄya atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ. Katamo eko dhammo? Sabbe sattÄ ÄhÄraá¹­á¹­hitikÄ. Sabbe sattÄ saá¹…khÄraá¹­á¹­hitikÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena eko dhammo sammadakkhÄto. 303.â€œBhikkhus, there is one Dhamma rightly proclaimed by the Blessed Oneâ€”the Knower, the Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. Herein, all should recite together, not dispute, so that this holy life may endure long and be long-lasting, for the welfare of the many, for the happiness of the many, out of compassion for the world, for the good, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans. What is that one Dhamma? All beings are sustained by nutriment. All beings are sustained by formations. This, bhikkhus, is that one Dhamma rightly proclaimed by the Blessed Oneâ€”the Knower, the Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. Herein, all should recite together, not dispute, so that this holy life may endure long and be long-lasting, for the welfare of the many, for the happiness of the many, out of compassion for the world, for the good, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans.â€

## Dukaá¹ƒ

304.Friends, there are two things rightly proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Knower and Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. Concerning these, all should recite together in concord, not dispute, so that this holy life may last long and endure for a long time, for the welfare and happiness of many people, out of compassion for the world, for the good, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans. What are these two?

Knowledge of destruction and knowledge of non-arising.

â€˜â€˜Ime kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena dve dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ. Tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒ, na vivaditabbaá¹ƒ, yathayidaá¹ƒ brahmacariyaá¹ƒ addhaniyaá¹ƒ assa ciraá¹­á¹­hitikaá¹ƒ, tadassa bahujanahitÄya bahujanasukhÄya lokÄnukampÄya atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ.

These, friends, are the two things rightly proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Knower and Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. Concerning these, all should recite together in concord, not dispute, so that this holy life may last long and endure for a long time, for the welfare and happiness of many people, out of compassion for the world, for the good, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans.

## Tikaá¹ƒ

## Catukkaá¹ƒ

### The Fours

306. â€˜â€˜Atthi kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena cattÄro dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ. Tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒ, na vivaditabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ. Katame cattÄro?

306.â€œThere are, friends, four things well proclaimed by the Blessed One, the knower, the seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. On these, all should chant together, not disputeâ€¦ for the welfare and happiness of devas and humans. What are the four?

â€˜â€˜CattÄro satipaá¹­á¹­hÄnÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu kÄye kÄyÄnupassÄ« viharati ÄtÄpÄ« sampajÄno satimÄ, vineyya loke abhijjhÄdomanassaá¹ƒ. VedanÄsu vedanÄnupassÄ«â€¦peâ€¦ citte cittÄnupassÄ«â€¦peâ€¦ dhammesu dhammÄnupassÄ« viharati ÄtÄpÄ« sampajÄno satimÄ vineyya loke abhijjhÄdomanassaá¹ƒ.

â€œThe four foundations of mindfulness. Here, friends, a monk dwells contemplating the body in the body, ardent, clearly comprehending, mindful, having removed covetousness and distress in the world. â€˜â€˜CattÄro sammappadhÄnÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu anuppannÄnaá¹ƒ pÄpakÄnaá¹ƒ akusalÄnaá¹ƒ dhammÄnaá¹ƒ anuppÄdÄya chandaá¹ƒ janeti vÄyamati vÄ«riyaá¹ƒ Ärabhati cittaá¹ƒ paggaá¹‡hÄti padahati. â€œThe four right strivings. â€œThe four jhÄnas. Here, friends, a monk, quite secluded from sensual pleasures, secluded from unwholesome states, enters and dwells in the first jhÄna, which is accompanied by thought and examination, with rapture and pleasure born of seclusion. 309.There are four noble lineages. Here, friends, a bhikkhu is content with any kind of robe, and he speaks in praise of contentment with any kind of robe. He does not engage in an uncalled-for and unsuitable search for a robe. If he does not obtain a robe, he is not anxious; if he obtains a robe, he uses it unattached, uninfatuated, unabsorbed, seeing the danger and understanding the escape. And because of this contentment with any kind of robe, he neither exalts himself nor disparages others. Whoever is expert, diligent, clearly comprehending, and mindful in this, friends, is called a bhikkhu standing in the ancient, foremost noble lineage.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu santuá¹­á¹­ho hoti itarÄ«tarena piá¹‡á¸apÄtena, itarÄ«tarapiá¹‡á¸apÄtasantuá¹­á¹­hiyÄ ca vaá¹‡á¹‡avÄdÄ«, na ca piá¹‡á¸apÄtahetu anesanaá¹ƒ appatirÅ«paá¹ƒ Äpajjati; aladdhÄ ca piá¹‡á¸apÄtaá¹ƒ na paritassati, laddhÄ ca piá¹‡á¸apÄtaá¹ƒ agadhito amucchito anajjhÄpanno ÄdÄ«navadassÄvÄ« nissaraá¹‡apaÃ±Ã±o paribhuÃ±jati; tÄya ca pana itarÄ«tarapiá¹‡á¸apÄtasantuá¹­á¹­hiyÄ nevattÄnukkaá¹ƒseti na paraá¹ƒ vambheti. 310. â€˜â€˜CattÄri padhÄnÄni. Saá¹ƒvarapadhÄnaá¹ƒ pahÄnapadhÄnaá¹ƒ bhÄvanÄpadhÄnaá¹ƒ [bhÄvanÄppadhÄnaá¹ƒ (syÄ.)] anurakkhaá¹‡ÄpadhÄnaá¹ƒ [anurakkhanÄppadhÄnaá¹ƒ (syÄ.)]. 310.There are these four efforts: the effort of restraint, the effort of abandoning, the effort of development, and the effort of preservation. And what, friends, is the effort of restraint? Here, friends, a bhikkhu, seeing a form with the eye, does not grasp at signs and features. By which, if he were to dwell with the eye-faculty unrestrained, evil unwholesome states of covetousness and distress might invade him, so he practices for its restraint, he guards the eye-faculty, he undertakes the restraint of the eye-faculty. Having heard a sound with the earâ€¦ having smelled an odor with the noseâ€¦ having tasted a flavor with the tongueâ€¦ having felt a tactile object with the bodyâ€¦ having cognized a mental object with the mind, he does not grasp at signs and features. By which, if he were to dwell with the mind-faculty unrestrained, evil unwholesome states of covetousness and distress might invade him, so he practices for its restraint, he guards the mind-faculty, he undertakes the restraint of the mind-faculty. This, friends, is called the effort of restraint.

â€˜â€˜KatamaÃ±cÄvuso, pahÄnapadhÄnaá¹ƒ? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu uppannaá¹ƒ kÄmavitakkaá¹ƒ nÄdhivÄseti pajahati vinodeti byantiá¹ƒ karoti [byantÄ« karoti (syÄ. kaá¹ƒ.)] anabhÄvaá¹ƒ gameti. Uppannaá¹ƒ byÄpÄdavitakkaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ uppannaá¹ƒ vihiá¹ƒsÄvitakkaá¹ƒâ€¦ uppannuppanne pÄpake akusale dhamme nÄdhivÄseti pajahati vinodeti byantiá¹ƒ karoti anabhÄvaá¹ƒ gameti. Idaá¹ƒ vuccatÄvuso, pahÄnapadhÄnaá¹ƒ.

And what, friends, is the effort of abandoning? Here, friends, a bhikkhu does not tolerate an arisen thought of sensual desire; he abandons it, dispels it, puts an end to it, annihilates it. He does not tolerate an arisen thought of ill willâ€¦ an arisen thought of crueltyâ€¦ any arisen evil unwholesome states; he abandons them, dispels them, puts an end to them, annihilates them. This, friends, is called the effort of abandoning.

â€˜â€˜KatamaÃ±cÄvuso, bhÄvanÄpadhÄnaá¹ƒ? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu satisambojjhaá¹…gaá¹ƒ bhÄveti vivekanissitaá¹ƒ virÄganissitaá¹ƒ nirodhanissitaá¹ƒ vossaggapariá¹‡Ämiá¹ƒ. 314.There are these four kinds of persons. Here, friend, a certain person is one who torments himself and is devoted to the practice of self-mortification. Here, friend, a certain person is one who torments others and is devoted to the practice of inflicting torment on others. Here, friend, a certain person is one who torments himself and is devoted to the practice of self-mortification, and torments others and is devoted to the practice of inflicting torment on others. Here, friend, a certain person is one who neither torments himself nor is devoted to the practice of self-mortification, nor torments others nor is devoted to the practice of inflicting torment on others. He, not tormenting himself or others, being without craving, extinguished, cooled, experiencing bliss in this very life, abides with a self that has become Brahma.

â€˜â€˜Aparepi cattÄro puggalÄ. IdhÄvuso, ekacco puggalo attahitÄya paá¹­ipanno hoti no parahitÄya. IdhÄvuso, ekacco puggalo parahitÄya paá¹­ipanno hoti no attahitÄya. IdhÄvuso, ekacco puggalo neva attahitÄya paá¹­ipanno hoti no parahitÄya. IdhÄvuso, ekacco puggalo attahitÄya ceva paá¹­ipanno hoti parahitÄya ca.

Furthermore, there are four other individuals. Here, friend, a certain individual is practicing for his own welfare, but not for the welfare of others. Here, friend, a certain individual is practicing for the welfare of others, but not for his own welfare. Here, friend, a certain individual is practicing neither for his own welfare nor for the welfare of others. Here, friend, a certain individual is practicing both for his own welfare and for the welfare of others.

â€˜â€˜Aparepi cattÄro puggalÄ â€“ tamo tamaparÄyano, tamo jotiparÄyano, joti tamaparÄyano, joti jotiparÄyano.

Furthermore, there are these four kinds of persons: one heading from darkness to darkness, one heading from darkness to light, one heading from light to darkness, one heading from light to light.

â€˜â€˜Aparepi cattÄro puggalÄ â€“ samaá¹‡amacalo, samaá¹‡apadumo, samaá¹‡apuá¹‡á¸arÄ«ko, samaá¹‡esu samaá¹‡asukhumÄlo.

Furthermore, there are these four kinds of persons: the unshakeable ascetic, the lotus-like ascetic, the white-lotus-like ascetic, the most delicate ascetic among ascetics.

â€˜â€˜Ime kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena cattÄro dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ; tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ.

These, friends, are the four qualities well proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, who knows and sees. Herein, all should recite in unisonâ€¦ for the welfare and happiness of devas and humans.

Paá¹­hamabhÄá¹‡avÄro niá¹­á¹­hito.

The first recitation section is concluded.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±cakkhandhÄ. RÅ«pakkhandho vedanÄkkhandho saÃ±Ã±Äkkhandho saá¹…khÄrakkhandho viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡akkhandho.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±cupÄdÄnakkhandhÄ. RÅ«pupÄdÄnakkhandho [rÅ«pÅ«pÄdÄnakkhandho (sÄ«. syÄ. kaá¹ƒ. pÄ«.) evamitaresupi] vedanupÄdÄnakkhandho saÃ±Ã±upÄdÄnakkhandho saá¹…khÄrupÄdÄnakkhandho viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡upÄdÄnakkhandho.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca macchariyÄni â€“ ÄvÄsamacchariyaá¹ƒ, kulamacchariyaá¹ƒ, lÄbhamacchariyaá¹ƒ, vaá¹‡á¹‡amacchariyaá¹ƒ, dhammamacchariyaá¹ƒ.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca nÄ«varaá¹‡Äni â€“ kÄmacchandanÄ«varaá¹‡aá¹ƒ, byÄpÄdanÄ«varaá¹‡aá¹ƒ, thinamiddhanÄ«varaá¹‡aá¹ƒ, uddhaccakukkuccanÄ«varaá¹‡aá¹ƒ, vicikicchÄnÄ«varaá¹‡aá¹ƒ.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca sikkhÄpadÄni â€“ pÄá¹‡ÄtipÄtÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, adinnÄdÄnÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, kÄmesumicchÄcÄrÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, musÄvÄdÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, surÄmerayamajjappamÄdaá¹­á¹­hÄnÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«.

316.The five impossibilities. A monk whose taints are destroyed is incapable, friend, of intentionally taking the life of a living being. A monk whose taints are destroyed is incapable of taking what is not given, in what is called theft. A monk whose taints are destroyed is incapable of engaging in sexual activity. A monk whose taints are destroyed is incapable of deliberately speaking a falsehood. A monk whose taints are destroyed is incapable of enjoying sensual pleasures after storing them up, as he did formerly when he was a householder.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca byasanÄni â€“ Ã±Ätibyasanaá¹ƒ, bhogabyasanaá¹ƒ, rogabyasanaá¹ƒ, sÄ«labyasanaá¹ƒ, diá¹­á¹­hibyasanaá¹ƒ. The five misfortunes: misfortune regarding relatives, misfortune regarding wealth, misfortune regarding disease, misfortune regarding virtue, misfortune regarding views. Friend, it is not because of misfortune regarding relatives, misfortune regarding wealth, or misfortune regarding disease that beings, with the breakup of the body, after death, reappear in a state of deprivation, a bad destination, the lower realms, or hell. But, friend, it is because of misfortune regarding virtue or misfortune regarding views that beings, with the breakup of the body, after death, reappear in a state of deprivation, a bad destination, the lower realms, or hell.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca sampadÄ â€“ Ã±ÄtisampadÄ, bhogasampadÄ, ÄrogyasampadÄ, sÄ«lasampadÄ, diá¹­á¹­hisampadÄ. The five drawbacks for one who is immoral, who is deficient in virtue. â€˜â€˜Codakena, Ävuso, bhikkhunÄ paraá¹ƒ codetukÄmena paÃ±ca dhamme ajjhattaá¹ƒ upaá¹­á¹­hapetvÄ paro codetabbo. Friend, a monk who wishes to admonish another should establish five qualities within himself before admonishing him. â€˜I will speak at the right time, not at the wrong time; I will speak truthfully, not untruthfully; I will speak gently, not harshly; I will speak beneficially, not unbeneficially; I will speak with a mind of loving-kindness, not with inner aversion.â€™ Friend, a monk who wishes to admonish another should establish these five qualities within himself before admonishing him.

317.There are five factors of striving. Here, friends, a bhikkhu is faithful; he trusts in the Tathagata's enlightenment: 'Indeed, the Blessed One is an Arahant, perfectly self-enlightened, accomplished in knowledge and conduct, fortunate, knower of the world, unsurpassed trainer of persons to be tamed, teacher of devas and humans, the Buddha, the Blessed One.' He is free from illness and affliction, possessing balanced digestion that is neither too cold nor too hot, but moderate and fit for striving. He is honest and sincere, not deceitful, revealing himself as he actually is to his teacher or to his wise companions in the holy life. He dwells with energy aroused for abandoning unwholesome qualities and for attaining wholesome qualities; firm, strong in effort, not neglecting his duty in wholesome qualities. And he is wise, possessing the wisdom of rise and fall, noble, penetrative, leading to the complete destruction of suffering.

318. â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca suddhÄvÄsÄ â€“ avihÄ, atappÄ, sudassÄ, sudassÄ«, akaniá¹­á¹­hÄ.

318.The five Pure Abodes are: Aviha, Atappa, Sudassa, Sudassi, and Akaniá¹­á¹­ha.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca anÄgÄmino â€“ antarÄparinibbÄyÄ«, upahaccaparinibbÄyÄ«, asaá¹…khÄraparinibbÄyÄ«, sasaá¹…khÄraparinibbÄyÄ«, uddhaá¹ƒsotoakaniá¹­á¹­hagÄmÄ«.

Five non-returners: one who attains NibbÄna in the interval, one who attains NibbÄna upon impact, one who attains NibbÄna without exertion, one who attains NibbÄna with exertion, and one who goes upstream to Akaniá¹­á¹­ha.

319.There are five barrennesses of mind. Here, friends, a bhikkhu has doubt and uncertainty about the Teacher, is not resolved, and lacks conviction. That bhikkhu, friends, who has doubt and uncertainty about the Teacher, is not resolved, and lacks convictionâ€”his mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion. For one whose mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion, this is the first barrenness of mind. Furthermore, friends, a bhikkhu has doubt and uncertainty about the Dhammaâ€¦ about the Sanghaâ€¦ about the trainingâ€¦ is angry and displeased with his fellow practitioners of the holy life, mentally hurt and resistant. That bhikkhu, friends, who is angry and displeased with his fellow practitioners of the holy life, mentally hurt and resistantâ€”his mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion. For one whose mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion, this is the fifth barrenness of mind.

320. â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca cetasovinibandhÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu kÄmesu avÄ«tarÄgo hoti avigatacchando avigatapemo avigatapipÄso avigatapariá¸·Äho avigatataá¹‡ho. Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu kÄye avÄ«tarÄgo hotiâ€¦peâ€¦ rÅ«pe avÄ«tarÄgo hotiâ€¦peâ€¦ puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu yÄvadatthaá¹ƒ udarÄvadehakaá¹ƒ bhuÃ±jitvÄ seyyasukhaá¹ƒ passasukhaá¹ƒ middhasukhaá¹ƒ anuyutto viharatiâ€¦peâ€¦ puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu aÃ±Ã±ataraá¹ƒ devanikÄyaá¹ƒ paá¹‡idhÄya brahmacariyaá¹ƒ carati â€“ â€˜iminÄhaá¹ƒ sÄ«lena vÄ vatena vÄ tapena vÄ brahmacariyena vÄ devo vÄ bhavissÄmi devaÃ±Ã±ataro vÄâ€™ti. Yassa cittaá¹ƒ na namati ÄtappÄya anuyogÄya sÄtaccÄya padhÄnÄya. Ayaá¹ƒ paÃ±camo cetaso vinibandho.

320.There are five mental bonds. Here, friends, a bhikkhu is not free from lust for sensual pleasures; he has not abandoned desire, affection, infatuation, burning, and craving for them. That bhikkhu, friends, who is not free from lust for sensual pleasuresâ€”who has not abandoned desire, affection, infatuation, burning, and craving for themâ€”his mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion. For one whose mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion, this is the first mental bond. Furthermore, friends, a bhikkhu is not free from lust for the body... not free from lust for forms... Furthermore, friends, a bhikkhu, having eaten his fill, is devoted to the pleasure of lying down, the pleasure of reclining, the pleasure of drowsiness... Furthermore, friends, a bhikkhu leads the holy life aspiring to some group of devas, thinking, 'By this virtue, observance, austerity, or holy life, I will become a deva or one of the devas.' That bhikkhu, friends, who leads the holy life aspiring to some group of devas, thinking, 'By this virtue, observance, austerity, or holy life, I will become a deva or one of the devas,' his mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion. For one whose mind does not incline toward ardency, dedication, constancy, and exertion, this is the fifth mental bond.

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±cindriyÄni â€“ cakkhundriyaá¹ƒ, sotindriyaá¹ƒ, ghÄnindriyaá¹ƒ, jivhindriyaá¹ƒ, kÄyindriyaá¹ƒ.

The five faculties are: the eye faculty, the ear faculty, the nose faculty, the tongue faculty, the body faculty.

â€˜â€˜AparÄnipi paÃ±cindriyÄni â€“ sukhindriyaá¹ƒ, dukkhindriyaá¹ƒ, somanassindriyaá¹ƒ, domanassindriyaá¹ƒ, upekkhindriyaá¹ƒ.

Furthermore, there are these other five faculties: the faculty of pleasure, the faculty of pain, the faculty of gladness, the faculty of sadness, and the faculty of equanimity.

â€˜â€˜AparÄnipi paÃ±cindriyÄni â€“ saddhindriyaá¹ƒ, vÄ«riyindriyaá¹ƒ, satindriyaá¹ƒ, samÄdhindriyaá¹ƒ, paÃ±Ã±indriyaá¹ƒ.

Furthermore, there are also these five faculties: the faculty of faith, the faculty of energy, the faculty of mindfulness, the faculty of concentration, and the faculty of wisdom.

321. â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca nissaraá¹‡iyÄ [nissÄraá¹‡Ä«yÄ (sÄ«. syÄ. kaá¹ƒ. pÄ«.) á¹­Ä«kÄ oloketabbÄ] dhÄtuyo. Tassa taá¹ƒ cittaá¹ƒ sugataá¹ƒ subhÄvitaá¹ƒ suvuá¹­á¹­hitaá¹ƒ suvimuttaá¹ƒ visaá¹ƒyuttaá¹ƒ kÄmehi. Ye ca kÄmapaccayÄ uppajjanti ÄsavÄ vighÄtÄ pariá¸·ÄhÄ [vighÄtapariá¸·ÄhÄ (syÄ. kaá¹ƒ.)], mutto so tehi, na so taá¹ƒ vedanaá¹ƒ vedeti. IdamakkhÄtaá¹ƒ kÄmÄnaá¹ƒ nissaraá¹‡aá¹ƒ.

321.There are five elements of escape. Here, friends, when a bhikkhu attends to sensual pleasures, his mind does not leap forward into sensual pleasures, does not become serene, does not become established, and does not become liberated. But when he attends to renunciation, his mind leaps forward into renunciation, becomes serene, becomes established, and becomes liberated. His mind is thus well-gone, well-developed, well-risen, well-liberated, and detached from sensual pleasures. And whatever taints, distress, and torments arise dependent on sensual pleasuresâ€”he is freed from them, he does not experience that feeling. This is declared as the escape from sensual pleasures.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno byÄpÄdaá¹ƒ manasikaroto byÄpÄde cittaá¹ƒ na pakkhandati na pasÄ«dati na santiá¹­á¹­hati na vimuccati. â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno rÅ«pe manasikaroto rÅ«pesu cittaá¹ƒ na pakkhandati na pasÄ«dati na santiá¹­á¹­hati na vimuccati. â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno sakkÄyaá¹ƒ manasikaroto sakkÄye cittaá¹ƒ na pakkhandati na pasÄ«dati na santiá¹­á¹­hati na vimuccati. 322. â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca vimuttÄyatanÄni. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhuno satthÄ dhammaá¹ƒ deseti aÃ±Ã±ataro vÄ garuá¹­á¹­hÄniyo sabrahmacÄrÄ«. YathÄ yathÄ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno satthÄ dhammaá¹ƒ deseti aÃ±Ã±ataro vÄ garuá¹­á¹­hÄniyo sabrahmacÄrÄ«. TathÄ tathÄ so tasmiá¹ƒ dhamme atthapaá¹­isaá¹ƒvedÄ« ca hoti dhammapaá¹­isaá¹ƒvedÄ« ca. Idaá¹ƒ paá¹­hamaá¹ƒ vimuttÄyatanaá¹ƒ.

322.â€œThere are five foundations for liberation. Here, friends, the Teacher teaches a bhikkhu the Dhamma, or else a respected fellow monastic. To the extent that the Teacher teaches a bhikkhu the Dhamma, or else a respected fellow monastic, to that extent he experiences the meaning and the Dhamma in that Dhamma. As he experiences the meaning and the Dhamma, joy springs up in him. Being joyful, rapture springs up in him. When his mind is filled with rapture, his body becomes tranquil. With his body tranquil, he feels happiness. Being happy, his mind becomes concentrated. This is the first foundation for liberation.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno na heva kho satthÄ dhammaá¹ƒ deseti aÃ±Ã±ataro vÄ garuá¹­á¹­hÄniyo sabrahmacÄrÄ«, api ca kho yathÄsutaá¹ƒ yathÄpariyattaá¹ƒ dhammaá¹ƒ vitthÄrena paresaá¹ƒ desetiâ€¦peâ€¦ api ca kho yathÄsutaá¹ƒ yathÄpariyattaá¹ƒ dhammaá¹ƒ vitthÄrena sajjhÄyaá¹ƒ karotiâ€¦peâ€¦ api ca kho yathÄsutaá¹ƒ yathÄpariyattaá¹ƒ dhammaá¹ƒ cetasÄ anuvitakketi anuvicÄreti manasÄnupekkhatiâ€¦peâ€¦ api ca khvassa aÃ±Ã±ataraá¹ƒ samÄdhinimittaá¹ƒ suggahitaá¹ƒ hoti sumanasikataá¹ƒ sÅ«padhÄritaá¹ƒ suppaá¹­ividdhaá¹ƒ paÃ±Ã±Äya. YathÄ yathÄ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno aÃ±Ã±ataraá¹ƒ samÄdhinimittaá¹ƒ suggahitaá¹ƒ hoti sumanasikataá¹ƒ sÅ«padhÄritaá¹ƒ suppaá¹­ividdhaá¹ƒ paÃ±Ã±Äya tathÄ tathÄ so tasmiá¹ƒ dhamme atthapaá¹­isaá¹ƒvedÄ« ca hoti dhammapaá¹­isaá¹ƒvedÄ« ca. Tassa atthapaá¹­isaá¹ƒvedino dhammapaá¹­isaá¹ƒvedino pÄmojjaá¹ƒ jÄyati, pamuditassa pÄ«ti jÄyati, pÄ«timanassa kÄyo passambhati, passaddhakÄyo sukhaá¹ƒ vedeti, sukhino cittaá¹ƒ samÄdhiyati. Idaá¹ƒ paÃ±camaá¹ƒ vimuttÄyatanaá¹ƒ.

â€œFurthermore, friends, a bhikkhuâ€™s Teacher or a respected fellow monastic does not teach him the Dhamma. But he teaches the Dhamma in detail to others as he has heard and memorized it. Or he recites the Dhamma in detail as he has heard and memorized it. Or he applies his mind to and examines and explores the Dhamma with his mind as he has heard and memorized it. Or he has a meditation subject that is well grasped, well attended to, well retained, and well penetrated by wisdom. As he experiences the meaning and the Dhamma, joy springs up in him. Being joyful, rapture springs up in him. When his mind is filled with rapture, his body becomes tranquil. With his body tranquil, he feels happiness. Being happy, his mind becomes concentrated. This is the fifth foundation for liberation.â€

â€˜â€˜PaÃ±ca vimuttiparipÄcanÄ«yÄ saÃ±Ã±Ä â€“ aniccasaÃ±Ã±Ä, anicce dukkhasaÃ±Ã±Ä, dukkhe anattasaÃ±Ã±Ä, pahÄnasaÃ±Ã±Ä, virÄgasaÃ±Ã±Ä.

â€œThere are five perceptions conducive to the ripening of liberation: the perception of impermanence, the perception of suffering in impermanence, the perception of non-self in suffering, the perception of abandoning, and the perception of dispassion.â€

â€˜â€˜Ime kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena paÃ±ca dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ; tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ [saá¹…gitiyapaÃ±cakaá¹ƒ niá¹­á¹­hitaá¹ƒ (syÄ. kaá¹ƒ.)].

## Chakkaá¹ƒ

### The Group of Six

323. â€˜â€˜Atthi kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena cha dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ; tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ. Katame cha?

323.â€œThere are, friends, six things well expounded by the Blessed One who knows and sees, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. In these, all should recite them in unison, without dispute, for the welfare and happiness of many, out of compassion for the world, for the good, welfare, and happiness of devas and humans. What are the six?

â€˜â€˜Cha ajjhattikÄni ÄyatanÄni â€“ cakkhÄyatanaá¹ƒ, sotÄyatanaá¹ƒ, ghÄnÄyatanaá¹ƒ, jivhÄyatanaá¹ƒ, kÄyÄyatanaá¹ƒ, manÄyatanaá¹ƒ.

â€œThe six internal sense bases are: the eye base, the ear base, the nose base, the tongue base, the body base, and the mind base.

â€˜â€˜Cha bÄhirÄni ÄyatanÄni â€“ rÅ«pÄyatanaá¹ƒ, saddÄyatanaá¹ƒ, gandhÄyatanaá¹ƒ, rasÄyatanaá¹ƒ, phoá¹­á¹­habbÄyatanaá¹ƒ, dhammÄyatanaá¹ƒ.

â€œThe six external sense bases are: the form base, the sound base, the smell base, the taste base, the tactile object base, and the mental-object base.

â€˜â€˜Cha viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡akÄyÄ â€“ cakkhuviÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ, sotaviÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ, ghÄnaviÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ, jivhÄviÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ, kÄyaviÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ, manoviÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ.

â€œThe six classes of consciousness: eye-consciousness, ear-consciousness, nose-consciousness, tongue-consciousness, body-consciousness, and mind-consciousness.â€

â€˜â€˜Cha phassakÄyÄ â€“ cakkhusamphasso, sotasamphasso, ghÄnasamphasso, jivhÄsamphasso, kÄyasamphasso, manosamphasso.

â€˜â€˜Cha vedanÄkÄyÄ â€“ cakkhusamphassajÄ vedanÄ, sotasamphassajÄ vedanÄ, ghÄnasamphassajÄ vedanÄ, jivhÄsamphassajÄ vedanÄ, kÄyasamphassajÄ vedanÄ, manosamphassajÄ vedanÄ.

â€œThe six classes of feeling: feeling born of eye-contact, feeling born of ear-contact, feeling born of nose-contact, feeling born of tongue-contact, feeling born of body-contact, and feeling born of mind-contact.

â€˜â€˜Cha saÃ±Ã±ÄkÄyÄ â€“ rÅ«pasaÃ±Ã±Ä, saddasaÃ±Ã±Ä, gandhasaÃ±Ã±Ä, rasasaÃ±Ã±Ä, phoá¹­á¹­habbasaÃ±Ã±Ä, dhammasaÃ±Ã±Ä.

â€˜â€˜Cha saÃ±cetanÄkÄyÄ â€“ rÅ«pasaÃ±cetanÄ, saddasaÃ±cetanÄ, gandhasaÃ±cetanÄ, rasasaÃ±cetanÄ, phoá¹­á¹­habbasaÃ±cetanÄ, dhammasaÃ±cetanÄ.

â€œSix classes of volition: volition regarding forms, volition regarding sounds, volition regarding smells, volition regarding tastes, volition regarding tactile objects, volition regarding mental phenomena.

â€˜â€˜Cha taá¹‡hÄkÄyÄ â€“ rÅ«pataá¹‡hÄ, saddataá¹‡hÄ, gandhataá¹‡hÄ, rasataá¹‡hÄ, phoá¹­á¹­habbataá¹‡hÄ, dhammataá¹‡hÄ.

â€œSix classes of craving: craving for forms, craving for sounds, craving for smells, craving for tastes, craving for tactile objects, craving for mental phenomena.

324. â€˜â€˜Cha agÄravÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu satthari agÄravo viharati appatisso; dhamme agÄravo viharati appatisso; saá¹…ghe agÄravo viharati appatisso; sikkhÄya agÄravo viharati appatisso; appamÄde agÄravo viharati appatisso; paá¹­isanthÄre [paá¹­isandhÄre (ka.)] agÄravo viharati appatisso.

324.â€œSix types of disrespect. â€˜â€˜Cha gÄravÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu satthari sagÄravo viharati sappatisso; dhamme sagÄravo viharati sappatisso; saá¹…ghe sagÄravo viharati sappatisso; sikkhÄya sagÄravo viharati sappatisso; appamÄde sagÄravo viharati sappatisso; paá¹­isanthÄre sagÄravo viharati sappatisso.

â€˜â€˜Cha somanassÅ«pavicÄrÄ. CakkhunÄ rÅ«paá¹ƒ disvÄ somanassaá¹­á¹­hÄniyaá¹ƒ rÅ«paá¹ƒ upavicarati; sotena saddaá¹ƒ sutvÄâ€¦ ghÄnena gandhaá¹ƒ ghÄyitvÄâ€¦ jivhÄya rasaá¹ƒ sÄyitvÄâ€¦ kÄyena phoá¹­á¹­habbaá¹ƒ phusitvÄ. ManasÄ dhammaá¹ƒ viÃ±Ã±Äya somanassaá¹­á¹­hÄniyaá¹ƒ dhammaá¹ƒ upavicarati.

â€œSix investigations connected with joy: Seeing a form with the eye, he investigates a form connected with joy; hearing a sound with the ear, he investigates a sound connected with joy; smelling an odor with the nose, he investigates an odor connected with joy; tasting a flavor with the tongue, he investigates a flavor connected with joy; touching a tactile object with the body, he investigates a tactile object connected with joy; cognizing a mental object with the mind, he investigates a mental object connected with joy.

â€˜â€˜Cha domanassÅ«pavicÄrÄ. CakkhunÄ rÅ«paá¹ƒ disvÄ domanassaá¹­á¹­hÄniyaá¹ƒ rÅ«paá¹ƒ upavicaratiâ€¦peâ€¦ manasÄ dhammaá¹ƒ viÃ±Ã±Äya domanassaá¹­á¹­hÄniyaá¹ƒ dhammaá¹ƒ upavicarati.

â€˜â€˜Cha upekkhÅ«pavicÄrÄ. CakkhunÄ rÅ«paá¹ƒ disvÄ upekkhÄá¹­á¹­hÄniyaá¹ƒ [upekkhÄá¹­hÄniyaá¹ƒ (ka.)] rÅ«paá¹ƒ upavicaratiâ€¦peâ€¦ manasÄ dhammaá¹ƒ viÃ±Ã±Äya upekkhÄá¹­á¹­hÄniyaá¹ƒ dhammaá¹ƒ upavicarati.

â€œSix investigations based on equanimity: Having seen a form with the eye, he investigates a form that is a basis for equanimity; having heard a sound with the ear, he investigates a sound that is a basis for equanimity; having smelled an odor with the nose, he investigates an odor that is a basis for equanimity; having tasted a flavor with the tongue, he investigates a flavor that is a basis for equanimity; having touched a tactile object with the body, he investigates a tactile object that is a basis for equanimity; having cognized a mental phenomenon with the mind, he investigates a mental phenomenon that is a basis for equanimity.

â€˜â€˜Cha sÄraá¹‡Ä«yÄ dhammÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhuno mettaá¹ƒ kÄyakammaá¹ƒ paccupaá¹­á¹­hitaá¹ƒ hoti sabrahmacÄrÄ«su Ävi [ÄvÄ« (ka. sÄ«. pÄ«. ka.)] ceva raho ca. Ayampi dhammo sÄraá¹‡Ä«yo piyakaraá¹‡o garukaraá¹‡o saá¹…gahÄya avivÄdÄya sÄmaggiyÄ ekÄ«bhÄvÄya saá¹ƒvattati.

â€œSix qualities that create affection and respect. Here, friends, a bhikkhu maintains bodily acts of loving-kindness towards his fellow monastics, both openly and in private. This quality creates affection and respect, conduces to cohesion, non-dispute, concord, and unity.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno mettaá¹ƒ vacÄ«kammaá¹ƒ paccupaá¹­á¹­hitaá¹ƒ hoti sabrahmacÄrÄ«su Ävi ceva raho ca. Ayampi dhammo sÄraá¹‡Ä«yoâ€¦peâ€¦ ekÄ«bhÄvÄya saá¹ƒvattati.

â€œFurthermore, friends, a bhikkhu maintains verbal acts of loving-kindness towards his fellow monastics, both openly and in private. This quality creates affection and respect, conduces to cohesion, non-dispute, concord, and unity.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhuno mettaá¹ƒ manokammaá¹ƒ paccupaá¹­á¹­hitaá¹ƒ hoti sabrahmacÄrÄ«su Ävi ceva raho ca. Ayampi dhammo sÄraá¹‡Ä«yoâ€¦peâ€¦ ekÄ«bhÄvÄya saá¹ƒvattati.

â€œFurthermore, friends, a bhikkhu maintains mental acts of loving-kindness towards his fellow monastics, both openly and in private. This quality creates affection and respect, conduces to cohesion, non-dispute, concord, and unity.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu ye te lÄbhÄ dhammikÄ dhammaladdhÄ antamaso pattapariyÄpannamattampi, tathÄrÅ«pehi lÄbhehi appaá¹­ivibhattabhogÄ« hoti sÄ«lavantehi sabrahmacÄrÄ«hi sÄdhÄraá¹‡abhogÄ«. Ayampi dhammo sÄraá¹‡Ä«yoâ€¦peâ€¦ ekÄ«bhÄvÄya saá¹ƒvattati.

â€œFurthermore, friends, any gains a bhikkhu has obtained in accordance with the Dhamma, even the contents of his alms bowl, he shares without reservation with his virtuous fellow monastics. This quality creates affection and respect, conduces to cohesion, non-dispute, concord, and unity.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu yÄni tÄni sÄ«lÄni akhaá¹‡á¸Äni acchiddÄni asabalÄni akammÄsÄni bhujissÄni viÃ±Ã±uppasatthÄni aparÄmaá¹­á¹­hÄni samÄdhisaá¹ƒvattanikÄni, tathÄrÅ«pesu sÄ«lesu sÄ«lasÄmaÃ±Ã±agato viharati sabrahmacÄrÄ«hi Ävi ceva raho ca. â€œFurthermore, friends, a bhikkhu dwells openly and in private sharing with his fellow monastics those virtues that are unbroken, flawless, unspotted, untarnished, liberating, commended by the wise, ungrasped at, and conducive to concentration. This quality creates affection and respect, conduces to cohesion, non-dispute, concord, and unity.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu yÄyaá¹ƒ diá¹­á¹­hi ariyÄ niyyÄnikÄ niyyÄti takkarassa sammÄ dukkhakkhayÄya, tathÄrÅ«pÄya diá¹­á¹­hiyÄ diá¹­á¹­hisÄmaÃ±Ã±agato viharati sabrahmacÄrÄ«hi Ävi ceva raho ca. 325. Cha vivÄdamÅ«lÄni. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu kodhano hoti upanÄhÄ«. 325.There are six roots of disputes. Here, friends, a bhikkhu is prone to anger and is resentful. That bhikkhu, friends, who is prone to anger and is resentful dwells without reverence or deference toward the Teacher, the Dhamma, and the Saá¹…gha, and is not a complete fulfiller of the training. Such a bhikkhu, friends, who dwells without reverence or deference toward the Teacher, the Dhamma, and the Saá¹…gha, and is not a complete fulfiller of the training, creates disputes in the Saá¹…gha. That dispute is for the harm and unhappiness of many people, for the disadvantage, harm, and suffering of devas and humans. If you, friends, perceive such a root of dispute either internally or externally, you should strive for the abandoning of that evil root of dispute. If you, friends, do not perceive such a root of dispute either internally or externally, you should practice so that this evil root of dispute does not arise in the future. Thus, there is the abandoning of this evil root of dispute. Thus, there is the non-arising of it in the future.

Furthermore, friends, a bhikkhu is disparaging and rivalrous... envious and stingy... crafty and deceitful... of evil desires and holding wrong views... clinging to his own views, tenacious in grasping, and difficult to relinquish. 328.Six constant abodes. Here, friends, a bhikkhu, having seen a form with the eye, is neither pleased nor displeased, but dwells equanimous, mindful, and clearly comprehending. 329.Six kinds of birth. Here, friends, a certain person born of dark birth gives rise to dark qualities. Here, friends, a certain person born of dark birth gives rise to bright qualities. ## Sattakaá¹ƒ

### The Sevens

330. â€˜â€˜Atthi kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena satta dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ; tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ. Katame satta?

330.There are, friends, seven qualities well proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Knower and Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One; these should all be recited in unison... for the welfare, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans. What are the seven?

â€˜â€˜Satta ariyadhanÄni â€“ saddhÄdhanaá¹ƒ, sÄ«ladhanaá¹ƒ, hiridhanaá¹ƒ, ottappadhanaá¹ƒ, sutadhanaá¹ƒ, cÄgadhanaá¹ƒ, paÃ±Ã±Ädhanaá¹ƒ.

The seven noble treasures: the treasure of faith, the treasure of virtue, the treasure of moral shame, the treasure of moral dread, the treasure of learning, the treasure of generosity, the treasure of wisdom.

â€˜â€˜Satta bojjhaá¹…gÄ â€“ satisambojjhaá¹…go, dhammavicayasambojjhaá¹…go, vÄ«riyasambojjhaá¹…go, pÄ«tisambojjhaá¹…go, passaddhisambojjhaá¹…go, samÄdhisambojjhaá¹…go, upekkhÄsambojjhaá¹…go.

The seven factors of enlightenment: the enlightenment factor of mindfulness, the enlightenment factor of investigation of the Dhamma, the enlightenment factor of energy, the enlightenment factor of rapture, the enlightenment factor of tranquility, the enlightenment factor of concentration, the enlightenment factor of equanimity.

â€˜â€˜Satta samÄdhiparikkhÄrÄ â€“ sammÄdiá¹­á¹­hi, sammÄsaá¹…kappo, sammÄvÄcÄ, sammÄkammanto, sammÄÄjÄ«vo, sammÄvÄyÄmo, sammÄsati.

The seven requisites for concentration: right view, right intention, right speech, right action, right livelihood, right effort, right mindfulness.

â€˜â€˜Satta asaddhammÄ â€“ idhÄvuso, bhikkhu assaddho hoti, ahiriko hoti, anottappÄ« hoti, appassuto hoti, kusÄ«to hoti, muá¹­á¹­hassati hoti, duppaÃ±Ã±o hoti.

The seven ignoble qualities: Here, friends, a bhikkhu is faithless, shameless, reckless, unlearned, lazy, unmindful, and unwise.

â€˜â€˜Satta saddhammÄ â€“ idhÄvuso, bhikkhu saddho hoti, hirimÄ hoti, ottappÄ« hoti, bahussuto hoti, ÄraddhavÄ«riyo hoti, upaá¹­á¹­hitassati hoti, paÃ±Ã±avÄ hoti.

The seven noble qualities: Here, friends, a bhikkhu is faithful, conscientious, scrupulous, learned, energetic, mindful, and wise.

â€˜â€˜Satta sappurisadhammÄ â€“ idhÄvuso, bhikkhu dhammaÃ±Ã±Å« ca hoti atthaÃ±Ã±Å« ca attaÃ±Ã±Å« ca mattaÃ±Ã±Å« ca kÄlaÃ±Ã±Å« ca parisaÃ±Ã±Å« ca puggalaÃ±Ã±Å« ca.

The seven qualities of a true person: Here, friends, a bhikkhu is one who knows the Dhamma, knows the meaning, knows the self, knows moderation, knows the time, knows the assembly, and knows individuals.

331. â€˜â€˜Satta niddasavatthÅ«ni. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu sikkhÄsamÄdÄne tibbacchando hoti, ÄyatiÃ±ca sikkhÄsamÄdÄne avigatapemo. DhammanisantiyÄ tibbacchando hoti, ÄyatiÃ±ca dhammanisantiyÄ avigatapemo. Diá¹­á¹­hipaá¹­ivedhe tibbacchando hoti, ÄyatiÃ±ca diá¹­á¹­hipaá¹­ivedhe avigatapemo.

331.Seven grounds for blamelessness: Here, friends, a bhikkhu has strong desire in undertaking the training, and in the future does not lose affection for undertaking the training. He has strong desire in penetrating the Dhamma, and in the future does not lose affection for penetrating the Dhamma. He has strong desire in eliminating desires, and in the future does not lose affection for eliminating desires. He has strong desire in seclusion, and in the future does not lose affection for seclusion. He has strong desire in initiating effort, and in the future does not lose affection for initiating effort. He has strong desire in mindfulness and prudence, and in the future does not lose affection for mindfulness and prudence. He has strong desire in penetrating views, and in the future does not lose affection for penetrating views.

â€˜â€˜Satta saÃ±Ã±Ä â€“ aniccasaÃ±Ã±Ä, anattasaÃ±Ã±Ä, asubhasaÃ±Ã±Ä, ÄdÄ«navasaÃ±Ã±Ä, pahÄnasaÃ±Ã±Ä, virÄgasaÃ±Ã±Ä, nirodhasaÃ±Ã±Ä.

Seven perceptions: the perception of impermanence, the perception of not-self, the perception of unattractiveness, the perception of drawback, the perception of abandoning, the perception of dispassion, the perception of cessation.

â€˜â€˜Satta balÄni â€“ saddhÄbalaá¹ƒ, vÄ«riyabalaá¹ƒ, hiribalaá¹ƒ, ottappabalaá¹ƒ, satibalaá¹ƒ, samÄdhibalaá¹ƒ, paÃ±Ã±Äbalaá¹ƒ.

Seven powers: the power of faith, the power of energy, the power of moral shame, the power of moral dread, the power of mindfulness, the power of concentration, the power of wisdom.

332. â€˜â€˜Satta viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hitiyo. SantÄvuso, sattÄ nÄnattakÄyÄ nÄnattasaÃ±Ã±ino, seyyathÄpi manussÄ ekacce ca devÄ ekacce ca vinipÄtikÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ paá¹­hamÄ viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hiti.

332.Seven stations of consciousness. There are, friends, beings diverse in body and diverse in perception, such as humans, some devas, and some beings in the states of deprivation. This is the first station of consciousness.

â€˜â€˜SantÄvuso, sattÄ nÄnattakÄyÄ ekattasaÃ±Ã±ino seyyathÄpi devÄ brahmakÄyikÄ paá¹­hamÄbhinibbattÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ dutiyÄ viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hiti.

There are, friends, beings diverse in body but unified in perception, such as the devas of BrahmÄâ€™s retinue who are newly reborn. This is the second station of consciousness.

â€˜â€˜SantÄvuso, sattÄ ekattakÄyÄ nÄnattasaÃ±Ã±ino seyyathÄpi devÄ ÄbhassarÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ tatiyÄ viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hiti.

There are, friends, beings unified in body but diverse in perception, such as the devas of streaming radiance. This is the third station of consciousness.

â€˜â€˜SantÄvuso, sattÄ ekattakÄyÄ ekattasaÃ±Ã±ino seyyathÄpi devÄ subhakiá¹‡hÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ catutthÄ« viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hiti.

â€˜â€˜SantÄvuso, sattÄ sabbaso rÅ«pasaÃ±Ã±Änaá¹ƒ samatikkamÄ paá¹­ighasaÃ±Ã±Änaá¹ƒ atthaá¹…gamÄ nÄnattasaÃ±Ã±Änaá¹ƒ amanasikÄrÄ â€˜ananto ÄkÄsoâ€™ti ÄkÄsÄnaÃ±cÄyatanÅ«pagÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ paÃ±camÄ« viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hiti.

There are, friends, beings who, with the complete surmounting of perceptions of form, with the disappearance of perceptions of sensory impingement, not attending to perceptions of diversity, (thinking,) â€˜Infinite is space,â€™ attain to the dimension of infinite space. This is the fifth station of consciousness.

â€˜â€˜SantÄvuso, sattÄ sabbaso ÄkÄsÄnaÃ±cÄyatanaá¹ƒ samatikkamma â€˜anantaá¹ƒ viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aâ€™nti viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aÃ±cÄyatanÅ«pagÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ chaá¹­á¹­hÄ« viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hiti.

There are, friends, beings who, completely transcending the dimension of infinite space, attain to the dimension of infinite consciousness, thinking, â€˜Consciousness is infinite.â€™ This is the sixth station of consciousness.

â€˜â€˜SantÄvuso, sattÄ sabbaso viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aÃ±cÄyatanaá¹ƒ samatikkamma â€˜natthi kiÃ±cÄ«â€™ti ÄkiÃ±caÃ±Ã±ÄyatanÅ«pagÄ. Ayaá¹ƒ sattamÄ« viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aá¹­á¹­hiti.

There are, friends, beings who, wholly transcending the dimension of infinite consciousness, attain to the dimension of nothingness, thinking, 'There is nothing.' This is the seventh station of consciousness.

â€˜â€˜Satta puggalÄ dakkhiá¹‡eyyÄ â€“ ubhatobhÄgavimutto, paÃ±Ã±Ävimutto, kÄyasakkhi, diá¹­á¹­hippatto, saddhÄvimutto, dhammÄnusÄrÄ«, saddhÄnusÄrÄ«.

Seven kinds of persons worthy of offerings: one liberated both ways, one liberated by wisdom, a body-witness, one attained to right view, one liberated by faith, a Dhamma-follower, a faith-follower.

â€˜â€˜Satta anusayÄ â€“ kÄmarÄgÄnusayo, paá¹­ighÄnusayo, diá¹­á¹­hÄnusayo, vicikicchÄnusayo, mÄnÄnusayo, bhavarÄgÄnusayo, avijjÄnusayo.

Seven underlying tendencies: the underlying tendency to sensual desire, the underlying tendency to aversion, the underlying tendency to views, the underlying tendency to doubt, the underlying tendency to conceit, the underlying tendency to craving for existence, the underlying tendency to ignorance.

â€˜â€˜Satta saÃ±Ã±ojanÄni â€“ anunayasaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ [kÄmasaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ (syÄ. kaá¹ƒ.)], paá¹­ighasaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ, diá¹­á¹­hisaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ, vicikicchÄsaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ, mÄnasaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ, bhavarÄgasaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ, avijjÄsaÃ±Ã±ojanaá¹ƒ.

Seven fetters: the fetter of attachment, the fetter of aversion, the fetter of views, the fetter of doubt, the fetter of conceit, the fetter of craving for existence, the fetter of ignorance.

â€˜â€˜Satta adhikaraá¹‡asamathÄ â€“ uppannuppannÄnaá¹ƒ adhikaraá¹‡Änaá¹ƒ samathÄya vÅ«pasamÄya sammukhÄvinayo dÄtabbo, sativinayo dÄtabbo, amÅ«á¸·havinayo dÄtabbo, paá¹­iÃ±Ã±Äya kÄretabbaá¹ƒ, yebhuyyasikÄ, tassapÄpiyasikÄ, tiá¹‡avatthÄrako.

Seven ways of settling disputes: settlement in the presence, settlement by mindfulness, settlement for one judged innocent, obtaining acknowledgment of the offense, decision by majority, adjudication of an obstinate offender, and covering over with grass.

â€˜â€˜Ime kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena satta dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ; tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ.

These, friends, are the seven qualities well proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Knower and Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One; these should all be recited in unison... for the welfare, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans.

DutiyabhÄá¹‡avÄro niá¹­á¹­hito.

The second recitation portion is concluded.

## Aá¹­á¹­hakaá¹ƒ

333.â€œFriends, there are eight qualities well-proclaimed by the Blessed One who knows and sees, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One; concerning which, all should recite in unisonâ€¦ for the benefit, welfare, and happiness of devas and humans. What are these eight?

â€˜â€˜Aá¹­á¹­ha micchattÄ â€“ micchÄdiá¹­á¹­hi, micchÄsaá¹…kappo, micchÄvÄcÄ, micchÄkammanto, micchÄÄjÄ«vo, micchÄvÄyÄmo micchÄsati, micchÄsamÄdhi.

â€˜â€˜Aá¹­á¹­ha puggalÄ dakkhiá¹‡eyyÄ â€“ sotÄpanno, sotÄpattiphalasacchikiriyÄya paá¹­ipanno; sakadÄgÄmÄ«, sakadÄgÄmiphalasacchikiriyÄya paá¹­ipanno; anÄgÄmÄ«, anÄgÄmiphalasacchikiriyÄya paá¹­ipanno; arahÄ, arahattaphalasacchikiriyÄya paá¹­ipanno.

â€˜â€˜Sabbaso rÅ«pasaÃ±Ã±Änaá¹ƒ samatikkamÄ paá¹­ighasaÃ±Ã±Änaá¹ƒ atthaá¹…gamÄ nÄnattasaÃ±Ã±Änaá¹ƒ amanasikÄrÄ â€˜ananto ÄkÄsoâ€™ti ÄkÄsÄnaÃ±cÄyatanaá¹ƒ upasampajja viharati. Ayaá¹ƒ catuttho vimokkho.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ majjhimesu janapadesu paccÄjÄto hoti. So ca hoti duppaÃ±Ã±o jaá¸·o eá¸·amÅ«go, nappaá¹­ibalo subhÄsitadubbhÄsitÄnamatthamaÃ±Ã±Ätuá¹ƒ. Ayaá¹ƒ aá¹­á¹­hamo akkhaá¹‡o asamayo brahmacariyavÄsÄya.

343. â€˜â€˜Nava anupubbavihÄrÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu vivicceva kÄmehi vivicca akusalehi dhammehi savitakkaá¹ƒ savicÄraá¹ƒ vivekajaá¹ƒ pÄ«tisukhaá¹ƒ paá¹­hamaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ upasampajja viharati. 343."There are these nine successive abodes. Here, friends, a bhikkhu, quite secluded from sensual pleasures, secluded from unwholesome states, enters and dwells in the first jhÄna, which is accompanied by applied thought and sustained thought, with rapture and pleasure born of seclusion. With the subsiding of applied thought and sustained thought, he enters and dwells in the second jhÄna, which has internal confidence and unification of mind, is without applied thought and sustained thought, and is filled with rapture and pleasure born of concentration. With the fading of rapture, he dwells in equanimity, mindful and clearly comprehending, and experiences pleasure with the body; he enters and dwells in the third jhÄna, of which the Noble Ones declare: â€˜He dwells in equanimity, mindful, and blissful.â€™ With the abandoning of pleasure and pain, and with the prior disappearance of joy and grief, he enters and dwells in the fourth jhÄna, which is neither painful nor pleasant and is purified by equanimity and mindfulness. With the complete transcending of the base of the infinity of consciousness, aware that â€˜there is nothing,â€™ he enters and dwells in the base of nothingness. With the complete transcending of the base of nothingness, he enters and dwells in the base of neither perception nor non-perception. With the complete transcending of the base of neither perception nor non-perception, he enters and dwells in the cessation of perception and feeling."

344. â€˜â€˜Nava anupubbanirodhÄ. Paá¹­hamaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpannassa kÄmasaÃ±Ã±Ä niruddhÄ hoti. Dutiyaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpannassa vitakkavicÄrÄ niruddhÄ honti. 344."There are nine successive cessations. For one who has attained the first jhÄna, perceptions of sensual desire have ceased. For one who has attained the second jhÄna, applied and sustained thought have ceased. For one who has attained the third jhÄna, rapture has ceased. For one who has attained the fourth jhÄna, in-breaths and out-breaths have ceased. For one who has attained the base of the infinity of space, perceptions of form have ceased. For one who has attained the base of the infinity of consciousness, perceptions of the base of the infinity of space have ceased. For one who has attained the base of nothingness, perceptions of the base of the infinity of consciousness have ceased. For one who has attained the base of neither perception nor non-perception, perceptions of the base of nothingness have ceased. For one who has attained the cessation of perception and feeling, perception and feeling have ceased."

â€˜â€˜Ime kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena nava dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ. Tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ.

"These, friends, are the nine qualities well-proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Knower, the Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. In these, all should recite together so that this holy life may be lasting and long-enduring, for the good of the many, for the happiness of the many, out of compassion for the world, for the good, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans."

## Dasakaá¹ƒ

### The Group of Ten

345. â€˜â€˜Atthi kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena dasa dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ. Tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒâ€¦peâ€¦ atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaá¹ƒ. Katame dasa?

345."There are, friends, ten qualities well-proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Knower, the Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. In these, all should recite together so that this holy life may be lasting and long-enduring, for the good of the many, for the happiness of the many, out of compassion for the world, for the good, benefit, and happiness of devas and humans. What are the ten?"

â€˜â€˜Dasa nÄthakaraá¹‡Ä dhammÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu sÄ«lavÄ hoti. PÄtimokkhasaá¹ƒvarasaá¹ƒvuto viharati ÄcÄragocarasampanno, aá¹‡umattesu vajjesu bhayadassÄvÄ« samÄdÄya sikkhati sikkhÄpadesu. Yaá¹ƒpÄvuso, bhikkhu sÄ«lavÄ hoti, pÄtimokkhasaá¹ƒvarasaá¹ƒvuto viharati, ÄcÄragocarasampanno, aá¹‡umattesu vajjesu bhayadassÄvÄ« samÄdÄya sikkhati sikkhÄpadesu. Ayampi dhammo nÄthakaraá¹‡o.

"Ten qualities that make one a refuge. Here, friends, a bhikkhu is virtuous. He dwells restrained by the PÄtimokkha restraint, endowed with good conduct and suitable resort, seeing danger in the slightest faults, and trains by undertaking the training rules. That a bhikkhu is virtuous, dwells restrained by the PÄtimokkha restraint, endowed with good conduct and suitable resort, seeing danger in the slightest faults, and trains by undertaking the training rulesâ€”this too is a quality that makes one a refuge."

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu bahussuto hoti sutadharo sutasannicayo. "Furthermore, friends, a bhikkhu is very learned, one who retains what he has heard, one who has accumulated what he has heard. â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu kalyÄá¹‡amitto hoti kalyÄá¹‡asahÄyo kalyÄá¹‡asampavaá¹…ko. Yaá¹ƒpÄvuso, bhikkhu kalyÄá¹‡amitto hoti kalyÄá¹‡asahÄyo kalyÄá¹‡asampavaá¹…ko. Ayampi dhammo nÄthakaraá¹‡o.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu dhammakÄmo hoti piyasamudÄhÄro, abhidhamme abhivinaye uá¸·ÄrapÄmojjo [uá¸·ÄrapÄmujjo (sÄ«. pÄ«.), oá¸·ÄrapÄmojjo (syÄ. kaá¹ƒ.)]. â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu santuá¹­á¹­ho hoti itarÄ«tarehi cÄ«varapiá¹‡á¸apÄtasenÄsanagilÄnappaccayabhesajjaparikkhÄrehi. Yaá¹ƒpÄvuso, bhikkhu santuá¹­á¹­ho hotiâ€¦peâ€¦ parikkhÄrehi. Ayampi dhammo nÄthakaraá¹‡o.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu ÄraddhavÄ«riyo viharati akusalÄnaá¹ƒ dhammÄnaá¹ƒ pahÄnÄya kusalÄnaá¹ƒ dhammÄnaá¹ƒ upasampadÄya, thÄmavÄ daá¸·haparakkamo anikkhittadhuro kusalesu dhammesu. "Furthermore, friends, a bhikkhu dwells with energy aroused for abandoning unwholesome qualities and acquiring wholesome qualities. â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu satimÄ hoti paramena satinepakkena samannÄgato cirakatampi cirabhÄsitampi saritÄ anussaritÄ. Yaá¹ƒpÄvuso, bhikkhu satimÄ hotiâ€¦peâ€¦ saritÄ anussaritÄ. Ayampi dhammo nÄthakaraá¹‡o.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, bhikkhu paÃ±Ã±avÄ hoti, udayatthagÄminiyÄ paÃ±Ã±Äya samannÄgato ariyÄya nibbedhikÄya sammÄdukkhakkhayagÄminiyÄ. Yaá¹ƒpÄvuso, bhikkhu paÃ±Ã±avÄ hotiâ€¦peâ€¦ sammÄdukkhakkhayagÄminiyÄ. Ayampi dhammo nÄthakaraá¹‡o.

346. Dasa kasiá¹‡ÄyatanÄni. PathavÄ«kasiá¹‡ameko saÃ±jÄnÄti, uddhaá¹ƒ adho tiriyaá¹ƒ advayaá¹ƒ appamÄá¹‡aá¹ƒ. 346."The ten kasina spheres. One perceives the earth kasinaâ€”above, below, across, without duality, boundless. One perceives the water kasinaâ€”above, below, across, without duality, boundless. One perceives the fire kasinaâ€”above, below, across, without duality, boundless. One perceives the air kasinaâ€”above, below, across, without duality, boundless. 347. â€˜â€˜Dasa akusalakammapathÄ â€“ pÄá¹‡ÄtipÄto, adinnÄdÄnaá¹ƒ, kÄmesumicchÄcÄro, musÄvÄdo, pisuá¹‡Ä vÄcÄ, pharusÄ vÄcÄ, samphappalÄpo, abhijjhÄ, byÄpÄdo, micchÄdiá¹­á¹­hi.

347."The ten unwholesome courses of action: killing living beings, taking what is not given, sexual misconduct, false speech, malicious speech, harsh speech, idle chatter, covetousness, ill will, wrong view."

â€˜â€˜Dasa kusalakammapathÄ â€“ pÄá¹‡ÄtipÄtÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, adinnÄdÄnÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, kÄmesumicchÄcÄrÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, musÄvÄdÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, pisuá¹‡Äya vÄcÄya veramaá¹‡Ä«, pharusÄya vÄcÄya veramaá¹‡Ä«, samphappalÄpÄ veramaá¹‡Ä«, anabhijjhÄ, abyÄpÄdo, sammÄdiá¹­á¹­hi.

"The ten wholesome courses of action: abstaining from killing living beings, abstaining from taking what is not given, abstaining from sexual misconduct, abstaining from false speech, abstaining from malicious speech, abstaining from harsh speech, abstaining from idle chatter, non-covetousness, non-ill will, right view."

348. â€˜â€˜Dasa ariyavÄsÄ. IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu paÃ±caá¹…gavippahÄ«no hoti, chaá¸·aá¹…gasamannÄgato, ekÄrakkho, caturÄpasseno, paá¹‡unnapaccekasacco, samavayasaá¹­á¹­hesano, anÄvilasaá¹…kappo, passaddhakÄyasaá¹…khÄro, suvimuttacitto, suvimuttapaÃ±Ã±o.

348."The ten noble abodes. Here, friends, a bhikkhu has abandoned five factors, possesses six factors, has a single guard, is supported by four things, has banished individual truths, has a quest thoroughly stilled, has thoughts free from disturbance, has bodily process tranquillized, is well liberated in mind, and well liberated in wisdom."

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu paÃ±caá¹…gavippahÄ«no hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhuno kÄmacchando pahÄ«no hoti, byÄpÄdo pahÄ«no hoti, thinamiddhaá¹ƒ pahÄ«naá¹ƒ hoti, uddhaccakukuccaá¹ƒ pahÄ«naá¹ƒ hoti, vicikicchÄ pahÄ«nÄ hoti. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu paÃ±caá¹…gavippahÄ«no hoti.

"And how, friends, is a bhikkhu one who has abandoned five factors? Here, friends, a bhikkhu has abandoned sensual desire, abandoned ill will, abandoned sloth and torpor, abandoned restlessness and remorse, abandoned doubt. Thus, friends, a bhikkhu is one who has abandoned five factors."

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu chaá¸·aá¹…gasamannÄgato hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu cakkhunÄ rÅ«paá¹ƒ disvÄ neva sumano hoti na dummano, upekkhako viharati sato sampajÄno. Sotena saddaá¹ƒ sutvÄâ€¦peâ€¦ manasÄ dhammaá¹ƒ viÃ±Ã±Äya neva sumano hoti na dummano, upekkhako viharati sato sampajÄno. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu chaá¸·aá¹…gasamannÄgato hoti.

"And how, friends, is a bhikkhu one who possesses six factors? Here, friends, a bhikkhu, having seen a form with the eye, is neither pleased nor displeased, but dwells equanimous, mindful, and clearly comprehending. Having heard a sound with the ear, he is neither pleased nor displeased, but dwells equanimous, mindful, and clearly comprehending. Having smelled a smell with the nose, he is neither pleased nor displeased, but dwells equanimous, mindful, and clearly comprehending. Having tasted a taste with the tongue, he is neither pleased nor displeased, but dwells equanimous, mindful, and clearly comprehending. Having felt a tactile sensation with the body, he is neither pleased nor displeased, but dwells equanimous, mindful, and clearly comprehending. Having cognized a mental object with the mind, he is neither pleased nor displeased, but dwells equanimous, mindful, and clearly comprehending. Thus, friends, a bhikkhu is one who possesses six factors."

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu ekÄrakkho hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu satÄrakkhena cetasÄ samannÄgato hoti. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu ekÄrakkho hoti.

"And how, friends, is a bhikkhu one who has a single guard? Here, friends, a bhikkhu is endowed with mindfulness as his guard. Thus, friends, a bhikkhu is one who has a single guard."

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu caturÄpasseno hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu saá¹…khÄyekaá¹ƒ paá¹­isevati, saá¹…khÄyekaá¹ƒ adhivÄseti, saá¹…khÄyekaá¹ƒ parivajjeti, saá¹…khÄyekaá¹ƒ vinodeti. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu caturÄpasseno hoti.

â€œAnd how, friends, does a bhikkhu have four supports? Here, friends, a bhikkhu reflects on one thing and uses it; reflects on one thing and endures it; reflects on one thing and avoids it; reflects on one thing and dispels it. It is in this way, friends, that a bhikkhu has four supports.â€

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu paá¹‡unnapaccekasacco hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhuno yÄni tÄni puthusamaá¹‡abrÄhmaá¹‡Änaá¹ƒ puthupaccekasaccÄni, sabbÄni tÄni nunnÄni honti paá¹‡unnÄni cattÄni vantÄni muttÄni pahÄ«nÄni paá¹­inissaá¹­á¹­hÄni. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu paá¹‡unnapaccekasacco hoti.

â€œAnd how, friends, does a bhikkhu have repelled individual truths? Here, friends, whatever numerous individual truths are held by numerous ascetics and brahminsâ€”all of them have been driven away, repelled, cast out, disgorged, released, abandoned, and relinquished by that bhikkhu. It is in this way, friends, that a bhikkhu has repelled individual truths.â€

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu samavayasaá¹­á¹­hesano hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhuno kÄmesanÄ pahÄ«nÄ hoti, bhavesanÄ pahÄ«nÄ hoti, brahmacariyesanÄ paá¹­ippassaddhÄ. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu samavayasaá¹­á¹­hesano hoti.

â€œAnd how, friends, does a bhikkhu have completely relinquished quests? Here, friends, a bhikkhu has abandoned the quest for sensual desires, abandoned the quest for being, and the quest for the holy life has been tranquilized. It is in this way, friends, that a bhikkhu has completely relinquished quests.â€

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu anÄvilasaá¹…kappo hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhuno kÄmasaá¹…kappo pahÄ«no hoti, byÄpÄdasaá¹…kappo pahÄ«no hoti, vihiá¹ƒsÄsaá¹…kappo pahÄ«no hoti. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu anÄvilasaá¹…kappo hoti.

â€œAnd how, friends, does a bhikkhu have unblemished intentions? Here, friends, a bhikkhu has abandoned sensual intentions, abandoned intentions of ill will, and abandoned intentions of harming. It is in this way, friends, that a bhikkhu has unblemished intentions.â€

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu passaddhakÄyasaá¹…khÄro hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu sukhassa ca pahÄnÄ dukkhassa ca pahÄnÄ pubbeva somanassadomanassÄnaá¹ƒ atthaá¹…gamÄ adukkhamasukhaá¹ƒ upekkhÄsatipÄrisuddhiá¹ƒ catutthaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ upasampajja viharati. â€œAnd how, friends, does a bhikkhu have tranquilized bodily formations? Here, friends, a bhikkhu, with the abandoning of pleasure and pain, and with the prior passing away of joy and sorrow, enters and dwells in the fourth jhÄna, which is neither painful nor pleasant and features the purity of mindfulness due to equanimity. â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu suvimuttacitto hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhuno rÄgÄ cittaá¹ƒ vimuttaá¹ƒ hoti, dosÄ cittaá¹ƒ vimuttaá¹ƒ hoti, mohÄ cittaá¹ƒ vimuttaá¹ƒ hoti. Evaá¹ƒ kho, Ävuso, bhikkhu suvimuttacitto hoti.

â€œAnd how, friends, is a bhikkhu well liberated in mind? Here, friends, a bhikkhuâ€™s mind is liberated from lust, liberated from hatred, and liberated from delusion. It is in this way, friends, that a bhikkhu is well liberated in mind.â€

â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±cÄvuso, bhikkhu suvimuttapaÃ±Ã±o hoti? IdhÄvuso, bhikkhu â€˜rÄgo me pahÄ«no ucchinnamÅ«lo tÄlÄvatthukato anabhÄvaá¹ƒkato Äyatiá¹ƒ anuppÄdadhammoâ€™ti pajÄnÄti. â€˜Doso me pahÄ«no ucchinnamÅ«lo tÄlÄvatthukato anabhÄvaá¹ƒkato Äyatiá¹ƒ anuppÄdadhammoâ€™ti pajÄnÄti. â€˜Moho me pahÄ«no ucchinnamÅ«lo tÄlÄvatthukato anabhÄvaá¹ƒkato Äyatiá¹ƒ anuppÄdadhammoâ€™ti pajÄnÄti. â€œAnd how, friends, is a bhikkhu well liberated by wisdom? Here, friends, a bhikkhu understands: â€˜My lust is abandoned, its root cut off, made like a palm stump, obliterated, and unable to arise in the future.â€™ He understands: â€˜My hatred is abandoned, its root cut off, made like a palm stump, obliterated, and unable to arise in the future.â€™ He understands: â€˜My delusion is abandoned, its root cut off, made like a palm stump, obliterated, and unable to arise in the future.â€™ It is in this way, friends, that a bhikkhu is well liberated by wisdom.â€

â€˜â€˜Dasa asekkhÄ dhammÄ â€“ asekkhÄ sammÄdiá¹­á¹­hi, asekkho sammÄsaá¹…kappo, asekkhÄ sammÄvÄcÄ, asekkho sammÄkammanto, asekkho sammÄÄjÄ«vo, asekkho sammÄvÄyÄmo, asekkhÄ sammÄsati, asekkho sammÄsamÄdhi, asekkhaá¹ƒ sammÄÃ±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ, asekkhÄ sammÄvimutti.

â€œThese are the ten qualities of one beyond training: right view of one beyond training, right thought of one beyond training, right speech of one beyond training, right action of one beyond training, right livelihood of one beyond training, right effort of one beyond training, right mindfulness of one beyond training, right concentration of one beyond training, right knowledge of one beyond training, and right liberation of one beyond training.â€

â€˜â€˜Ime kho, Ävuso, tena bhagavatÄ jÄnatÄ passatÄ arahatÄ sammÄsambuddhena dasa dhammÄ sammadakkhÄtÄ. Tattha sabbeheva saá¹…gÄyitabbaá¹ƒ na vivaditabbaá¹ƒ, yathayidaá¹ƒ brahmacariyaá¹ƒ addhaniyaá¹ƒ assa ciraá¹­á¹­hitikaá¹ƒ, tadassa bahujanahitÄya bahujanasukhÄya lokÄnukampÄya atthÄya hitÄya sukhÄya devamanussÄnaâ€™â€™nti.

â€œThese, friends, are the ten qualities well proclaimed by the Blessed One, the Knower and Seer, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One. Concerning these, all should recite together in concord, without dispute, so that this holy life may last long and endure long, for the welfare of the many, for the happiness of the many, out of compassion for the world, for the good, welfare, and happiness of devas and humans.â€

349. Atha kho bhagavÄ uá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ Äyasmantaá¹ƒ sÄriputtaá¹ƒ Ämantesi â€“ â€˜sÄdhu sÄdhu, sÄriputta, sÄdhu kho tvaá¹ƒ, sÄriputta, bhikkhÅ«naá¹ƒ saá¹…gÄ«tipariyÄyaá¹ƒ abhÄsÄ«â€™ti. 349.Then the Blessed One rose from his seat and addressed Venerable SÄriputta: â€œGood, good, SÄriputta! Saá¹…gÄ«tisuttaá¹ƒ niá¹­á¹­hitaá¹ƒ dasamaá¹ƒ.
